SUBJECT: Paul Arnold PIERROCT - Background Information provided by
Air Attache, Leopoldville
1
N'DOLO airport is currently being evacuated by the U.K.O.C.
forces and turned over to the Cenzolese government for use by the
Concloses Air Force There are some 150 cadets who have received some
training and are considered ready for advanced training, but as of this
time, have nowhere to be trained PIERROCT has made extensive efforts
to obtain aid from many sources to train these cadets The AIRA re-
searcher of the U.K.O.C. has been given a religious, the British,
United Nations, and asked the AIRA to request aid in the U.K.O.C. for
the Cenzolese Air Force, About 30 cadets a.e in training in Tunisia at
the present time. On 11 March the AIRA recommended aid be extended to
the Cenzolese Air Force, but under the auspices of the United Nations,
2 PIERROCT also reported 11 March that he had 6 Koth and 9 Har-
vard T-5 aircraft being delivered near the end of Karch, and asked if
the United Nations Command would allow them to enter the-Congo, He
even offered to let the planes remain under U.N. control.
3 PIERROCT is a mulatto ad claimo to have a white grandmother
in Dallas, Texas He was trained by the Belgians and claims to have
known 0-471's and T-33 jet planes, though he has not been on flying sta-
tions. He was a very good leader in the U.K.O.C. and was a very good
is not available His assistant is Lt L.J. LEXA' who is reportedly
completely devoted to PIERROCT PIERROCT is personally ambitious and at
one point in the fall of 1960, he approached FREEIDE authorities with
a plan to take over the government if they would help him His plan
was too transparent and weck for any serious consideration at that
time.

A. DIR 25730
B. ABL4 630 dated 19 October 1961
1- On 29 November 1961-11000UA told the underaiged that he felt his
position vis-a-vis the Congolese Government was repaily weakening. First,
WIEGUS had endorsed sending one of the advisors with the Congolese Air
Force to Europe to purchase planes and later found WIEARV/4 was at least
vocianat of a second GOZ representative sent to Europe on the same mission.
The 1961-11000UA was a 1961-11000UA. The Congolese Prance of the
40,000,000 available for airplane purchases "good" and 1961-11000UA
WIEGUS was incensed at the move of the GOO in sending a parallel mission
to Europe and not informing him of it. He saw WIEARV/2 and asked about
this other mission. WIZARD/2 apparently informed WIZARD/4 about
WIEGUS's visit and since then, for a period of the last five days,
WIZARD/3, 1961-11000UA.
2. The GOO has also a;;arently proposed sending WINDOWS on an
intelligence gathering mission to Katanga. WIEGUS asked all FURBAK were
interested in this undertooking. We advised him strongly about this
move and added we had no interest whatsoever in the project.
3. WIEGUS has also met the ODOATH representative and showed him
the model submarine which was the subject of ABLA-630. The ODOATH
representative evinced interest in this model and through the ODUAIT
representative, whom WIEGUS has seen on several occasions and discussed
with the following plans for the GOO, the ODOATH representative
was aware that WIEGUS was a 1961-11000UA to discuss alonged by WIZARD/2 to
travel to PPEKINGS. He said for the ODOATS to inform his when he was ready
to depart and he would arrange with ODOATS to contact appropriate ODOATH
people in PPEKING to discuss the model.
4. WIEGUS a:proached GUTHEALI on November 24 and SALVACK on November
29 with a request whother he might be of use to KUBARK either in Africa
at the elsewhere in the world, and that he would like to be taken back into
the world. He said for the ODOATS to about his position in the GOO at this
time and feels with the diplomatic relations of the U.S. and the U.S. and
Belgium and the GOO that his position will become increasingly weaker. To
reemphasize past assessments of WIEGUS, he is far too disorganized an
individual to be an effective PI Agent but would probably be useful where
action is required but detailed accurate reporting is not. The station
agrees with only statement made concerning WIEGUS that he has a
peculiar turn of which lends itself remarkably to nafarious and
extra-legal activities but would add that these activities should be of
an action type.

13 September 1961
GENERAL
On T September 1961, the SUBJECT, David TIZTICIONVILI, and Case
Officer Dan H. wore not by the reporting agent at the Union Station in
Washington, D. C. at 0930 hours. At this time the case officer ax-
plained to the SUBJECT that the Union Station sought would have in his
poessesion documents for SUBJECT and two and dollars in cash
which was to be given to SUBJECT after their agreement. Frankfurt,
Germany. At this time the SUBJECT executed a signed receipt for the
money and documents and this receipt was kept by the case.
The SUBJECT and reporting agent departed Union Station, Washington,
D. C. via Pennsylvania Railroad Train #174, the Colonial, and arrived
at Trenton, New Jersey, at 1300 hours, 7 September 1961. The SUBJECT
and reporting agent then proceeded via taxi-cab, Trenton, New Jersey, to
Exhalle Air Force Base, Whittsatown, New Jersey.
The SUBJECT and reporting agent departed McGuire Air Force Base
from Military Air Transport Service H&J 31 at 2000 hours and arrived in
February, Germany, at 0830 hours at the Rhein-Main Airport on 8 September
1961.
After arrival at Rhein-Main Airport SUBJECT and the reporting agent
proceeded via taxi-cab to downtown Frankfurt. At this time the money and
documents were given to SUBJECT. He executed a dated receipt for this
material which is attached to this report as Exhibit 8A. After SUBJECT
received the documents and money he departed the company of the reporting
agent at the train station in Frankfurt, Germany.
During the course of the trip to Germany SUBJECT stated that he would
possibly assist in Germany for a few weeks and that he was also contemplating
moving to South Central or returning to the Congo. SUBJECT seemed well satis-
fied with the termination agreement and at no time displayed any dissatis-
faction concerning his treatment during the past several months.
The reporting agent departed Frankfurt, Germany via Pan American
Airlines Flight, $73 et 3400 hours, 11 September 1961, and arrived at
Washington, D. C. at 1939 hours, 11 September 1961.
This flight covered a distance of approximately eight thousand miles
and the flight time was approximately seventeen hours.

1. CAJEEP-2 PHONED AT WIESBADEN HOME BY FOB STAFFER ASHR.
RIEDER ON 14 APRIL. HE AGREED INFORM US WHEN CONTRACT SIGNED AND ON
FUTURE TRAVEL.
2. ON 17 APRIL CAJEEP-2 PHONED TO CONFIRM HE LEAVING FOR MIDDLE
EAST. HAD HEARD NOTHING ABOUT CONTRACT BUT PRESUMES WILL BE SIGNED
BEFORE HIS RETURN TO WIESBADEN CIRCA 1 MAY.
3. WOULD APPRECIATE MORE DETAILS ON REF B REQUEST FOR RECRUITMENT
OF SELECTED CONGO JOB APPLICANTS. ADVISE LANGUAGE CAPABILITY DESIRED
OR SPECIFIC CRITERIA FOR PROPOSED RECRUITMENT ATTEMPTS WITH
GUIDANCE ON SALARY COMMITMENTS AND OPERATIONAL OBJECTIVES.

AND FLYING INSTRUCTOR PRIOR TO ARRIVAL LEOP. FULLY APPRECIATE TIME FACTOR
AND DESIRE PREEMPT ANY EFFORT ON PART PIERROT TO PROCURE INSTRUCTORS
BY OTHER CHANNELS. I'F WIROGUE AND SWANSON SETTLE ON NAMES THERE IS
IS POSSIBLE TIME FOR HQS TO CHECK OUT PROSPECTIVE INSTRUCTORS AND
MAKE RECRUITMENT PITCH. ALTHOUGH CONGOLESE HAVE BIG IDEAS AND
HOPE NEED MORE INSTRUCTORS, THIS MAY NOT BE CASE. IF WE RUSH IN ALL
NONKUBARK ASSETS WE MAY FIND OURSELVES WITH EXPENSIVE OP
OVER WHICH WE HAVE LITTLE CONTROL AND WHICH MIGHT PRODUCE LITTLE
FOR KUBARK.
4. IF FEASIBLE SUGGEST HQS DELAY SWANSON TRIP AND HAVE HIM CABLE
WIROGUE IMMEDIATELY TO MEET HIM IN EUROPE. ALSO, PLEASE ADVISE
SECRET
RFPRODUCTION BY OTHER THAN ISSUING OFFICE IS PROHIBITED

SECRET
DOCUMENTATION: PCR GEORO FEINER
Prit 104.43
MILITARY CONNIFICATE
1. Military Certificate issued by the 5th Grenndier Training Brigade. (Infustry)
The designation O.U. on the right hand- toy corner means "Ortsunterhunft", it is
the place of issue-which during var time did not specify a town or area due to
security consideration. It merely means the place where the unit was physically
stained at the time the document was issued. The certificate states that Capt.
Georg Reinier, born 25. July 1921 in Salzburg has lost his regular military pay
book on 2:2.1944 on account of encay action. A new book has not yet been issued.
SOLDSUCH ERSATZ
2. The Saldbuch Ersatz (Pay book substitute). (a) Front Section (Soldbuch-
Eracts) indicates that document was issued to Capt. Georg Reinier, born on 25.
July 1921 in Salzburg, his dog tag number is 214739, has nearest of kin, his
father Franz Reinier, lives in Ealsburg, Siebenburgerstri. 2. (b) The Section
(Orden und Ehrenzeichen) indicates that he received a medal for having been
vounded on 9.12.42. (c) The Section (Eurulerübungen über finat Tage) shows that
he was granted a leave for over five days. It was a convalescent leave which
entitled him to fire transportation. The lover portion of the same section indicates
that he received some shoots for dyneatery (Rull) and was vaccinated. The other aide
of the document shows the following from right to left.
a. Clothing record.
b. Issuance of retained slaving cream and scap.
c. Have of military unit to which he belongs.
3. It is requested that subject sign document on space provided. (Soldbuch
Erstat sure over Eigenhändige Unteroschrift.)
DO NOC use ball point pen. Have subject practice "his name" several times before
affixing to document.

GENÉRAL INFORMATION TO BE NOTED
Subject was issued the following documents:
1. Australian (Ordinary) Response No. 56.262 in Vienna at the main Passport
Office located in Vienna I, Postage 05, Vichir is near the main Post Office and also near
Schwedenplatz. As noted in the passport criteria of the German and German
valid until 1960, when it was again renewed for another five years. The lack of use
and entry cachets of very frequent travel to Germany and Berlin is explained by the fact
that generally since late 1955 Austrians entering Germany no longer were stamped in or
out. For this reason, Subject can claim that he made many trips to Germany and back
to the German and German who were registered in the special permits. (Austrians need
a residence permit only when they remain more than three years) and the
As noted above, that passport was first issued by the main Passport office, however,
the renewal was obtained at a sub station, Wien IV, Taubstrümmengasse II. This can
be explained by the fact that at that time subject lived in that part of Vienna after
he returned from Berlin.
2. Austrian Drivers Permit:
This document was obtained in Vienna in 1956 and is valid for an indefinite
time. Section B, which is not crossed out indicates that he is authorized to drive
ordinary private cars not in excess of 3500 kg. (No trucks etc.) Reverse left hand
portion shows free stamp of 6 schilling has been paid. Normally this section also
indicates authority on which permit was issued, but since this is his first permit no
such entry is made.
3. International Certificate of Vaccination:
When subject contemplated travel outside Europe, he felt it best to
obtain a vaccination certificate normally required in many countries. He could have
obtained the blank document from a travel agency who directed him to go and have proper
entries made for smallpox and yellow fever. At the suggestion of the travel agency he
went to see Dr. Ladialus Township, General Prectitioner, Wien III, Markblannergasse 133.
This Doctor, had the necessary vaccines for smallpox and yellow fever and he took both
sections on 12 November 1959. Schulpox vaccinations are generally valid for three years.
The yellow fever shots are good for 6 years.
4. Baptismal Certificate:
This document was issued in Salzburg, the place where subject was born.
During the war years subject lost all his papers and so in 1958 he
returned to Salzburg to obtain a copy of his baptismal certificate. Entries indicate
that certificate was issued to Subject showing his fathers name as Reiner, Franz,
catholic, Geologist having lived at time of subjects birth in Salzburg, Siebenburgerstr.
2, that his father was born on 24. 4. 1899 in Vienna and that he was married in Vienna
on 23. 6. 1920.
Entries for his mother indicate her name as Maria Anna, nee Niclitz,
catholic, born on 20 August 1960 in Vienna.
The name of subjects God-Parent was Walter Kiener, who also was a
catholic and his professoria was Engineer from Slazburg. The priest who performed the
baptism was Erich Iegertz, Caelplain. The document was dated 23 August 1954 in Salzburg-
Millegs.

5. Letter indicated acceptance for employment in West Berlin.
For business reasons in accordance with cover legend, subject has been
in and out of Germany ever since 1955. By 1958 subject became interested in seeking
employment in Berlin. He was in contact with the construction firm of Arthur Doll
and Son and after he wrote to them on 24. 7. 58 he received a reply that this firm was
willing to give him a job as an engineer. Since he indicated in his letter to the firm
that the was about to come to Berlin anyway, the firm of Doll suggested to him that he
should stop at their office and sign a formal work contract.

EXPLAICATION OF THE PASSPORT ENTRIES
Inside front cover: Contains cachet indicating that Subject paid 20 Schilling
to obtain passport.
PAGE 1: This page contains Passport Serial "B" Nr. 54626. The Dues Stamp of
6 Schilling also indicates payment despite the fact that the opposite
page shows 20 Schilling. This is the normal procedure. The payment
number is the accession number of the passport office and the last type
number indicate that the document was issued in 1955. Further entries
indicate name and profession and nationality of bearer to be Austrian.
PAGE 2: Entries on this page indicate the following: Occupation as Engineer,
that the was born in Salzburg or 25 July 1921, his present place of
residence is Vienna. It is further indicated that the shape of his
case was similar, his eyes brown and hair color brown. Special identifications
marks and the form his thumb and index finger are missing.
PAGE 3: This page shows the picture of the bearer including the dry seal for
authentication over the picture. Below is the space for subject to
affix his signature. The bottom of the page shows a wet authenticating
seal and the signature of the display. Who issued the document.
PAGE 4: This page indicates that the passport is valid for all countries of the
world, that it is valid until 25 August 1960 and was issued in Vienna
on 26 August 1955. The last entry indicates that passport was renewed
until 24 August 1965 for such entry please see page 13.
PAGES
These pages show various entry and exit cachets of simulated travel
5, 6,
undertaken by subject. (For further explanations see attached sheet
& 7:
for travel.)
PAGE 9: This entry is a residence permit for West Berlin and valid for three
months. (Austriens normally don't need a permit for any stay in Germany
unless they stay more than three months.) This permit was obtained in
West Berlin from Div. II Berlin Police. The fee paid was one IV. It
was invalidated when a new residence permit was obtained.
PAGE 11: This page indicates a second residence permit for Berlin which was placed
in the passport when the permit on page 9 expired. It was validated for
six months at this time, and again the fee was one IM. Valid from 10 June
until 11 December 1960.
PAGE 13: This page indicates that the Passport was revalidated in Vienna at the
Police Station at Vienna-Wieden. This Police Station is located at
Thubstumengasse 11, Wien IV, and is located west of the Schwarzenberger
Park. Entry shows 6 Schilling fiscal stamp, but a payment of 10 Schilling
had to be made for revalidation. Document is valid until 24 August 1965.
